<Review>Prices are expected. Quality was much better before they remodeled and changed the menu. The cups are thin, if your drink takes any fall it will likely split on the side. The variety of popping boba is fun. If you like boba pearls but hate the slimy stuff on them, this is a good choice. Sample as much as you can before you commit to a drink, it's not easy nor hard to order something you'll hate. I'm not wild about this place, but it does fill that occasional craving.

I've never tried the forever yogurt because it looks sketch.</Review>< time>

Gabe Estrella</name>
<Time>1523485560629<//Time>< Rating>
5<//Rating>
<Text>As of April 2018, this place is reopen. Bee&Tea is still around, however, Forever Yogurt (the froyo) has been replaced with Juice Zone (I guess Forever Yogurt wasn't actually forever -_-). Juice Zone offers smoothies, fresh juices, and similar items. That portion of the restaurant opens at 8AM. The Bee&Tea portion, which seems to serve the same boba teas and food ( like the 1 pound "Asian" wrap), opens at 10AM. They both close at 10PM.

As of October 2017, this place seems to now be closed, which in a way I'm not surprised...every time I came here, I seemed to only 1 of 3 customers at lunch time.

I don't have any complaints about the yogurt, teas, or food. I like that this place is walking distance from work, so I did enjoy coming here for lunch. I would usually order the huge 1 pound wraps that were a little bigger than the size of my two fists. Everything about it tasted fresh, though sometimes I did feel like I ate too much (1lb in one sitting lol), and wish there was a smaller version. There were plenty of options for yogurt and toppings, and plenty of options for tea. The boba was the right consistency, not mushy or hard.

Anyway, I think the business would have been more successful if the parking lot had an exit at the end so a right turn can be made behind the building (there is already an access road there for other businesses behind Bee&Tea), and from there one could turn onto North Main. As it is, the parking lot force turns you into the awkward Geary Rd, where you then have to go into the Sprouts parking lot and exit their back way to turn into the reverse direction of Geary Rd in order get back onto North Main or Treat Blvd.

I hope this is not the end for Bee & Tea, as I do miss having lunch here.</Text><Pics>None</Pics>< Resp>
None<//Resp>

I was looking for a pediatric dentist near town and after reviewing their reviews I decided to give them a shot and I was not disappointed.

I called to get an appointment for my son and the front desk was extremely helpful over the phone and what was my favorite thing was that they text me to confirm the appointment and emailed me as well. Also, I really appreciated the link to fill out the new patient forms, that for me was awesome especially since I have two kids that was extremely helpful and it got it out the way for our scheduled appointment.

We arrived to our appointment and I think we waited less than two minutes and my son and I went in, he of course went to the small kids door which was pretty neat and I went thru the adult door. The whole experience was great. Robin catered to his needs of comfort and explained everything to him. After he got seen he was able to get a free toy as a reward for being good for his visit.

My son is 3 so this great for a parent of  two young children. He really became so comfortable that he liked her and was sad to leave.

Also, the cost for the initial visit was  explained very thoroughly and any other questions I had were answered. The front desk was extremely friendly and outgoing.

They have a tv for them to watch while their little teeth are being examined and there's a a little area in the lobby area for kids to play.

Me as a parent I also wanted to make sure I can be there for him when he gets examined, x ray, cleaning and I'm glad they allow that it puts me at ease.

I really recommend them! Our first time went great  and I can't wait for my little one to go here too.</Text>

< Text>
I love coming here, and to their original churreria (which is right down the street). The personnel is always friendly and the place is always clean! The small parking lot is a little inconvenient, but I don't mind too much as most people are in and out in less than 10 min. And they always have the mini cakes, which we buy at least 4 times a year. Today I purchased a 3 leches mini cake to celebrate my son's birthday. Looks so yummy, and it is very cute!</Text>

< Review>
Churros are 0.50 each! These churros aren't small at all. They're the size of the ones they sell at concession stands. They also sell churro rellenos which is churros filled with chocolate, cream, vanilla or guava for $1.50.

The churros are warm and covered in cinnamon sugar. Texture is good but just a bit hard .. not as soft and fresh like what I'm used to. But it is better than what you can find at amusement parks and WAY cheaper.

Parking here is TERRIBLE. Only 3-4 spots and you basically have to go in and back out the entrance to exit.<//Review>

< Review>
This is Marin's only large auditorium to see anyone involved in music, drama or comedy.  Greatest event that goes each year here is Singers Marin annual Holiday Concert. Comprised of four adult groups, four youth groups on stage singing the traditional, standard holiday music along with selections for the Hanukkah season.  Last year they did a few gospel tunes which brought the house down.

I always tell people if this don't put you in the holiday spirit than nothing will.

I've gone every year and it's an incredible show! Get your tickets to their show called, Tis The Season Cheers!  You won't regret it!<//Review>

<Text>Just had my first experience at this venue and I would say it's just okay. The place is huge for a veterans memorial hall and the outside and grounds are beautiful.

Appearance wise, It looks very nice inside as well, but the parking is ridiculous for sold out performances. We had to go  blocks away from the venue to get a space in one of their "onsite" lots, but did everyday find one. After the show it was a standing traffic jam to get out, which took close to an hour.

The Box Office line was a block long and under staffed, leaving many of us who came "early" rushing to get to our seats before the performance began. They definitely have "nose bleed" seats in this auditorium, high enough that you have a little trouble hearing the lower speaking on stage and you can see the performers, but not their facial details.

The Seats themselves were not very comfortable, but they did have ushers to help you find yours in the darkened theatre.

Not anxious to see another performance here, but It's give it one more try before giving up on it.<//Text>< Date>

<Name>Johnny Wang</Name><Pictures>None< /Pictures><text>My first experience with the MVMA (and Marin, for that matter) was a mere two months ago or so, coming up this way for a Jake Shimabukuro concert with a girl I was dating at the time. If you've never heard of the man, Youtube him: he does magic with a ukulele!

While positive overall, I did have a few mixed opinions about the venue. Let's start with the most important part of a venue for a musical performance: the sound system and setup here was fantastic. For those who care about lighting and effects, theirs were also surprisingly nice: no, not EDM show level impressive, but, very nice for small and solo acts.

As for the venue itself, while the outside and lobbies were quite nice, a careful glance around the auditorium itself showed that the place was definitely a little dated. To each their own on how to react to that: perhaps it's nostalgic and has character - to me, it just felt a little old and worn. That aside, the interior is fairly spacious, and performances without many (or any) intermissions won't notice that the two lobbies on either side are actually quite small, which was only noticeable to us because of the meet and greet Jake did after the show.

***Accessibility Info***

Venue - For a venue of their size, I was actually a little surprised at the amount of accessible wheelchair seating they had. Located roughly in the middle of the auditorium, where one of the main walkways was, were a smattering of spaces designated as wheelchair... parking spaces, if you will, with some adjacent seating reserved for accompanying guests.

Bathroom - I believe there were a set of bathrooms on each side of the auditorium. Either way, there is at least one that is perfectly accessible.</text><gmapID>0x808599d4c457465f:0x15468ca1c8b12e87< /gmapID>< date>

< Review>
K&H dental has been hands down the best dental experience of my life.

The staff is polite, cheerful and helpful, and the facilities are surprisingly comfortable. I've never had to wait much more than 10-15 minutes to be seen, and the doctor is extremely efficient and skilled.

My first visit, I had 5 teeth in need of extraction, most of which had become horribly infected and were excruciatingly painful. K&H was able to get me an appointment the same day in a little over an hour.  In about 5 minutes, they had me numbed up and comfortable. The doctor was with me 5 minutes after that, and had all my teeth extracted in under 10 minutes.

My next visit was for a root canal. I should mention that i have had two root canals in the past, and they were both long, uncomfortable, and painful experiences. Dr. Kaou was able to complete the procedure without any pain (aside from the novacaine shot) in about 20 minutes. 5 hours later, I can't even really tell I had any dental work done - it's not even a little sore.

I Strongly recommend K&H. They are skilled, polite, and professional.<//Review>

<userid>103924675123002294114< /userid><user_name>Christan Chanelle<//user_name><GmapID>0x80c2b882b5222d0b:0x2ff023586660adb8<//GmapID></record></dataset><record>

<Name>Melanie Tam< /Name>< date>
1518760940757< /date>
<rate>2< /rate><review>After a few attempts at other Korean BBQ restaurants on a Saturday night at 8, Yang San Bak was the only one that didn't require a wait. I guess that couldn't have been a good sign.

Three hangry friends and I went with the Combo C (for 3-4 people). For $64.99, you get brisket, rib belly, marinated beef, steak, and a bottle of soju. Between this and all of the banchan dishes, we were stuffed. It was more than enough food. The flavor of the meats and the side dishes were good overall, but some of the cuts were a bit chewy.

Service was lacking. I'm not sure if it's a Yang San Bak thing, or an LA KBBQ thing, but in NYC KBBQ spots, they help you cut up the meats, grill them, switch out your grill plate, and refill your banchan dishes. None of that happened here. We were left to handle our own meats, like peasants. And sadly, our empty banchan dishes went unfilled (waiters were nowhere to be found). I looked over at the couple next to us, and their grill was completely burnt, so it wasn't just our table.

I think next time, I'll get a snack to hold me over and wait it out at the better KBBQ restaurants.</review>< Pictures>

<text>Yum! This place is great. The food is good and the price is right. Definitely coming back for more.< /text><pics>None</pics><Response>None< /Response><Gmap_id>0x80c2b882b5222d0b:0x2ff023586660adb8< /Gmap_id></record>

<rating>5</rating><Review>The Place: It's located in a typical LA plaza with tiny parking and random stores and restaurants. However, what isn't typical, is the fact the place itself is fairly quiet. Club music isn't blaring at 96db. You can ACTUALLY talk to the person across the table in a normal voice. If you, or someone you know has a hearing aid and love KBBQ, please go to Yang San Bak.

The Food: High quality meats and delicious sides. So let's be honest, it doesn't have the best meat, but it does have great meat at a great price. It also has one of dipping sauces ever. Seriously, that red chili sauce is amazing.

The Price: This has one of the best quality to price ratios for a KBBQ place in Koreatown. And their combo/meal includes an alcoholic drink. So this makes the place even more reasonable if you drink but hate having to pay $12 for a bottle of soju.

What I Would Change: So this place isn't as hip or trendy as the other places in KTown. But this has become one of the best overall KBBQ places to go. It isn't as busy or packed as other KBBQ places in the area. It does make me worry if they're making enough business (given the rising rents). But then again, I like that we can go at 7PM and not have to wait until 8PM to finally be seated. So maybe I don't want anything to change about this place.< /Review>< Pictures>
None</Pictures>

The service is very Asian, speak up if you want anything or else you'll be ignored. We ordered a 2-3 person set, brisket, pork belly, rib fingers and bulgogi.
